###xml 766 775 766 775 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4A</bold></xref>
###xml 795 801 795 801 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HCP5-G</italic>
###xml 871 880 871 880 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4C</bold>
###xml 871 880 871 880 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4C</bold></xref>
###xml 993 999 993 999 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HCP5-G</italic>
###xml 1106 1114 1106 1114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-B*57</italic>
###xml 1119 1125 1119 1125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-C5</italic>
###xml 1126 1128 1126 1128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">-C</italic>
###xml 1224 1232 1224 1232 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-B*57</italic>
###xml 1237 1242 1237 1242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HCP5G</italic>
###xml 1325 1331 1325 1331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HCP5-G</italic>
###xml 1409 1416 1409 1416 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Table 2</bold>
###xml 1409 1416 1409 1416 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0003636-t002"><bold>Table 2</bold></xref>
Subjects with a B*57 allele were assigned to genotypic groups 1 to 3, but despite containing a B*57 allele, these genotypic groups were associated with contrasting disease-influencing effects (Figure 4B). Compared to subjects assigned to genotypic groups 1 or 3, those in group 2 had a faster rate of disease progression (Figure 4B). The distribution of the HCP5-G allele in group 2 revealed that individuals assigned to this group could be stratified into two broad categories, with subgroups 2A and 2B possessing or lacking a HCP5-G allele, respectively (Figure 4A). Remarkably, none of the 10 subjects categorized to group 2B progressed to AIDS (Figure 4C), and they all had a genotype that contained a HLA-B*57 and a HLA-C5'-C allele but lacked a HCP5-G allele (Figure 4A). By contrast, the HCP5-G-carrying subjects categorized to group 2A had a progressive disease (Figure 4C). The differential disease outcomes associated with groups 2A and 2B indicated that genotypes which contained a HCP5-G allele associated with disease acceleration despite containing two separate 'protective' alleles namely a HLA-B*57 and HLA-C5'-C allele (group 2A). Thus, the genotype-phenotype relationship for group 2A (which contains both HLA-B*57 and HCP5G alleles) may explain why when examined in a multivariate model, possession of the HCP5-G allele was associated with both disease acceleration and higher viral loads (Table 2, model 6).
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 64 73 64 73 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4B</bold>
###xml 64 73 64 73 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4B</bold></xref>
###xml 111 117 111 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-C5</italic>
###xml 118 120 118 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">-C</italic>
###xml 135 139 135 139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 196 205 196 205 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4B</bold>
###xml 196 205 196 205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4B</bold></xref>
###xml 288 294 288 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HCP5-G</italic>
###xml 335 339 335 339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 394 400 394 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HCP5-G</italic>
###xml 471 477 471 477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-C5</italic>
###xml 478 480 478 480 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">-C</italic>
###xml 490 499 490 499 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4B</bold>
###xml 490 499 490 499 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4B</bold></xref>
###xml 552 556 552 556 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Gonzalez1">[34]</xref>
###xml 558 562 558 562 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Mangano1">[41]</xref>
The phenotype of subjects in group 3 was also very instructive (Figure 4B). These subjects were homozygous for HLA-C5'-C and possessed B*57 and had among the slowest rates of disease progression (Figure 4B). This occurred despite the fact that most subjects in group 3 also possessed the HCP5-G allele. Thus, among those who possessed B*57, the disease-accelerating effects associated with the HCP5-G allele was evident in those with one (group 2A) but not two (group 3) HLA-C5'-C alleles (Figure 4B). These observations underscore our previous thesis [34], [41] that analyses conducted at the allele level obscure complex genotype-phenotype relationships that occur when the phenotypic effects of both haplotypes are accounted for.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 65 73 65 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-B*57</italic>
###xml 142 147 142 147 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-C</italic>
###xml 282 286 282 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 321 327 321 327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-C5</italic>
###xml 328 330 328 330 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">-T</italic>
###xml 439 445 439 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-C5</italic>
###xml 446 448 446 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">-C</italic>
###xml 492 500 492 500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-B*57</italic>
###xml 585 589 585 589 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 686 691 686 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57-</italic>
###xml 725 733 725 733 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4</bold>
###xml 725 733 725 733 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4</bold></xref>
###xml 733 736 733 736 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">, B</bold>
###xml 741 742 741 742 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</bold>
These survival curves also underscore two other points: First, a HLA-B*57-containing genotype does not require the presence of a 'protective' HLA-C allele to convey a protective effect on disease progression. This is reflected by the observation that subjects in group 1 who have a B*57 allele and are homozygous for the HLA-C5'-T allele have a slow disease course. Second, the maximal 'protective' effects associated with possession of a HLA-C5'-C allele occurs only when it is present in a HLA-B*57-containing genotype. This is reflected by the observation that subjects assigned to B*57-containing genotypic groups 2B or 3 have a much slower disease course than those categorized to B*57-lacking genotypic groups 5 and 6 (Figure 4, B and C, compare survival curves for groups 2B and 3 vs those for groups 5 and 6).
###end p 65
###begin title 66
B*57-containing genotypes and progressive disease
###end title 66
###begin p 67
###xml 122 126 122 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 161 165 161 165 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Migueles2">[20]</xref>
###xml 167 171 167 171 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Navis1">[22]</xref>
###xml 173 177 173 177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Bailey1">[42]</xref>
###xml 242 251 242 251 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4B</bold>
###xml 242 251 242 251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4B</bold></xref>
###xml 256 265 256 265 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4C</bold>
###xml 256 265 256 265 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4C</bold></xref>
###xml 327 335 327 335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-B*57</italic>
There is clinical, virologic and immunologic data indicating a conundrum: some subjects despite possessing a 'protective' B*57 have a progressive disease course [20], [22], [42]. We surmised that the genotype-phenotype relationships shown in Figure 4B and Figure 4C might address this paradox as they showed that subjects with HLA-B*57-containing genotypes classify into two categories.
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 182 190 182 190 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4</bold>
###xml 182 190 182 190 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4</bold></xref>
###xml 190 199 190 199 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">, B and C</bold>
###xml 258 262 258 262 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 280 289 280 289 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4D</bold>
###xml 280 289 280 289 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4D</bold></xref>
###xml 314 318 314 318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 425 429 425 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 469 470 469 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 479 481 479 481 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;5</sup>
###xml 483 492 483 492 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4D</bold>
###xml 483 504 483 504 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4D</bold>, left panel</xref>
###xml 570 579 570 579 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4D</bold>
###xml 570 591 570 591 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4D</bold>, left panel</xref>
###xml 720 724 720 724 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Dolan1">[39]</xref>
###xml 726 730 726 730 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-He1">[43]</xref>
The first group are those subjects with genetic features present in genotypic groups 1, 2B or 3 as these genotypic groups are associated with a non-progressive disease (NPD) course (Figure 4, B and C), and collectively these genotypes are designated here as B*57-NPD genotypes in Figure 4D. In the overall cohort, B*57-NPD genotypes conferred a nearly 83% slower rate of disease progression compared to genotypes that lack a B*57 allele (RH = 0.17, 95% CI = 0.07-0.41, P = 7.2x10-5; Figure 4D, left panel). These associations detected at the level of the entire cohort (Figure 4D, left panel) remained consistent after adjustment for covariates known to influence disease progression in this cohort, including ethnicity [39], [43].
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 88 92 88 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 235 244 235 244 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4D</bold>
###xml 235 244 235 244 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4D</bold></xref>
###xml 294 301 294 301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57-PD</italic>
###xml 342 346 342 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 355 364 355 364 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4D</bold>
###xml 355 364 355 364 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4D</bold></xref>
###xml 483 484 483 484 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 540 549 540 549 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4D</bold>
###xml 540 549 540 549 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4D</bold></xref>
###xml 549 550 549 550 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">;</bold>
###xml 652 661 652 661 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure S4</bold>
###xml 652 661 652 661 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0003636.s005"><bold>Figure S4</bold></xref>
###xml 716 724 716 724 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57-NPD</italic>
###xml 816 820 816 820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 860 861 860 861 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 480 483 <span type="species:ncbi:12721?0.9873544761140104">HIV</span>
The second group are those subjects categorized to group 2A and, compared to those with B*57-NPD genotypes, the clinical course of subjects in this group is characterized by a progressive disease (PD; designated as B*57-PD genotype in Figure 4D). Remarkably, the disease course of those with a B*57-PD genotype is similar to those who lack a B*57 allele (Figure 4D). Consistent genotype-phenotype relationships were also evident when similar analyses were conducted separately in HIV+ EAs and AAs before and after adjusting for covariates (Figure 4D; middle and right panels) or when the analyses were restricted to subjects who did not receive HAART (Figure S4). In these HAART-free subjects, those assigned to the B*57-NPD genotypic group had a nearly 80% lower risk of progressing to AIDS than those who lacked a B*57 allele (RH = 0.21; 95% CI = 0.08-0.57; P = 0.002).
###end p 69
###begin p 70
###xml 92 93 92 93 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 238 242 238 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 248 252 248 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 276 280 276 280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 412 413 412 413 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 477 481 477 481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 487 491 487 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 513 517 513 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 519 528 519 528 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4E</bold>
###xml 519 528 519 528 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4E</bold></xref>
###xml 570 574 570 574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 580 584 580 584 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 606 610 606 610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 674 683 674 683 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4E</bold>
###xml 674 683 674 683 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4E</bold></xref>
###xml 751 752 751 752 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 791 795 791 795 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 804 808 804 808 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 896 900 896 900 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 909 918 909 918 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4E</bold>
###xml 909 918 909 918 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4E</bold></xref>
Based on the aforementioned findings we surmised that the comparison of the immunologic (CD4+ T cell profiles and DTH skin test reactivity) and virologic (viral load) profiles would reveal a step-wise worsening in subjects categorized to B*57-NPD, B*57-PD and those lacking a B*57 allele. In general agreement with this, as a general rule, there was a step-wise decrease in the baseline, cumulative and nadir CD4+ T cell counts as well as DTH responses in subjects assigned to B*57-NPD, B*57-PD and those lacking B*57 (Figure 4E). Conversely, in subjects categorized to B*57-NPD, B*57-PD and those lacking B*57 there was a step-wise increase in the steady-state viral load (Figure 4E). The only exception to this general rule was that the baseline CD4+ T cell counts in subjects assigned to B*57-NPD and B*57-PD were similar, but they were higher than the cell counts found in those who lacked a B*57 allele (Figure 4E).
###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 17 21 17 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 422 426 422 426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 448 457 448 457 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 3D</bold>
###xml 448 457 448 457 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g003"><bold>Figure 3D</bold></xref>
###xml 509 513 509 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 541 545 541 545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 558 565 558 565 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57-PD</italic>
###xml 662 671 662 671 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4F</bold>
###xml 662 671 662 671 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4F</bold></xref>
###xml 848 852 848 852 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 942 946 930 934 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 961 970 949 958 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4F</bold>
###xml 961 982 949 970 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4F</bold>, left panel</xref>
###xml 1003 1012 991 1000 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4F</bold>
###xml 1003 1012 991 1000 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4F</bold></xref>
###xml 1202 1207 1190 1195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57-</italic>
###xml 1279 1283 1267 1271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 1387 1396 1373 1382 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4F</bold>
###xml 1387 1396 1373 1382 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4F</bold></xref>
###xml 1434 1443 1420 1429 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4F</bold>
###xml 1434 1443 1420 1429 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4F</bold></xref>
###xml 1499 1503 1485 1489 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 1530 1534 1516 1520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 1543 1547 1529 1533 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 1617 1621 1603 1607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 99 102 <span type="species:ncbi:12721?0.9873544761140104">HIV</span>
###xml 764 767 <span type="species:ncbi:12721?0.9873544761140104">HIV</span>
To validate that B*57-containing NPD and PD genotypes convey contrasting phenotypic effects during HIV disease course we used a complementary approach and determined the distributions of these genotypes as a function of increasing AIDS-free status and steady-state viral loads with the intent of testing two premises. First, although increasing AIDS-free status is associated with a stepwise enrichment of subjects with a B*57-containing genotype (Figure 3D), the greatest enrichment should be for those with B*57-NPD genotypes. Second, the B*57-NPD and not B*57-PD genotypes should be enriched for subjects with a low steady-state viral load. The data shown in Figure 4F (left panel) provides evidence in support for the first premise. Nearly 12 percent of those HIV-positive individuals who were AIDS-free after 10 years of follow-up possessed a B*57-containing genotype, and strikingly approximately90% of these subjects were those with a B*57-NPD genotype (Figure 4F, left panel). The data shown in Figure 4F (right panel) provides evidence in support of the second premise as among subjects with a steady-state viral load lower than 10,000 copies/ml, there was an overrepresentation of those with B*57-NPD genotypes. It was noteworthy that the proportion of subjects with a B*57-PD genotype was similar in those who had a steady-state viral load of <10,000 and >/=55,000 copies/ml (Figure 4F). Thus, these distribution patterns (Figure 4F) provide additional validity for the categorization of B*57-containing genotypes into B*57-NPD and B*57-PD genotypes as a means to improve the accuracy of identifying those B*57-carrying subjects who may have a slower disease course or control of viral replication during the early phases of infection.
###end p 71
###begin title 72
Viral load-independent effects of B*57-NPD genotypes
###end title 72
###begin p 73
###xml 104 108 104 108 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Mellors1">[28]</xref>
###xml 110 114 110 114 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Mellors2">[29]</xref>
###xml 184 188 184 188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 490 494 478 482 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Dolan1">[39]</xref>
###xml 635 636 623 624 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 675 679 663 667 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Rodriguez1">[44]</xref>
###xml 681 685 669 673 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0003636-Henry1">[45]</xref>
###xml 883 890 871 878 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Table 4</bold>
###xml 883 890 871 878 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0003636-t004"><bold>Table 4</bold></xref>
###xml 910 918 898 906 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-B*57</italic>
Based on the well-established, strong relationship between steady-state viral load and AIDS development [28], [29], one interpretation of the aforementioned findings might be that the B*57-NPD genotypes convey disease-retardation by simply influencing the extent of early viral replication. However, in a recent study, we found that although the steady-state viral load is a strong predictor of AIDS risk, it accounted for only approximately12% of the variability in AIDS progression rates [39]. The findings by Rodriguez et al also suggest that the contribution of viral load to the explained variability in the rate of decline in CD4+ T cell counts might not be very large [44], [45]. These data indicated that parameters that are independent of viral load are also critical determinants of AIDS pathogenesis. We therefore used nested multivariate Cox proportional hazards models (Table 4) to assess whether HLA-B*57-NPD genotypes affected disease progression independent of the viral load.
###end p 73
###begin title 74
###xml 54 62 54 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-B*57</italic>
Viral load-independent disease-influencing effects of HLA-B*57-containing genotypes.
###end title 74
###begin p 75
###xml 143 144 143 144 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">*</sup>
###xml 142 146 142 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B<sup>*</sup>57</italic>
###xml 155 156 155 156 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">*</sup>
###xml 154 158 154 158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B<sup>*</sup>57</italic>
###xml 340 341 340 341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 415 416 415 416 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">*</sup>
###xml 414 418 414 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B<sup>*</sup>57</italic>
###xml 473 474 473 474 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">*</sup>
###xml 472 476 472 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B<sup>*</sup>57</italic>
###xml 513 514 513 514 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">*</sup>
###xml 512 516 512 516 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B<sup>*</sup>57</italic>
###xml 587 588 587 588 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">*</sup>
###xml 586 590 586 590 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B<sup>*</sup>57</italic>
###xml 628 629 628 629 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">*</sup>
###xml 627 631 627 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B<sup>*</sup>57</italic>
###xml 710 719 710 719 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 4D</bold>
###xml 710 719 710 719 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0003636-g004"><bold>Figure 4D</bold></xref>
Results are from nested multivariate Cox proportional hazards models for the outcome of time to AIDS (1987 criteria) for subjects assigned to B*57-PD and B*57-NPD before (none, model 1) and after adjustment for covariates individually (models 2 to 6) or in unison (models 7 to 10). Data is presented as relative hazard (RH) with 95% CI and P values. The reference group for all the comparisons is those who lack a B*57 allele (relative hazard = 1). N, number of subjects. B*57-PD represents subjects who possess B*57-containing genotypes that associate with progressive disease whereas B*57-NPD represents subjects who possess B*57-containing genotypes that associate with non-progressive disease (as shown in Figure 4D).
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 87 95 87 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57-NPD</italic>
###xml 191 199 179 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-B*57</italic>
###xml 239 246 227 234 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Table 4</bold>
###xml 239 246 227 234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0003636-t004"><bold>Table 4</bold></xref>
###xml 484 488 472 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 581 588 569 576 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Table 4</bold>
###xml 581 588 569 576 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0003636-t004"><bold>Table 4</bold></xref>
###xml 680 687 668 675 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57-PD</italic>
###xml 708 712 696 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
###xml 754 761 742 749 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Table 4</bold>
###xml 754 761 742 749 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0003636-t004"><bold>Table 4</bold></xref>
###xml 857 864 845 852 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Table 4</bold>
###xml 857 864 845 852 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0003636-t004"><bold>Table 4</bold></xref>
###xml 51 54 <span type="species:ncbi:12721?0.9873544761140104">HIV</span>
###xml 64 71 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">persons</span>
Before accounting for any of the covariates, those HIV-positive persons categorized to B*57-NPD had an approximately83% lower risk of progressing to AIDS compared to individuals who lacked a HLA-B*57 allele (RH = 0.17; 95% CI = 0.07-0.41; Table 4, model 1). We next adjusted-individually and in unison-for the disease-influencing effects of several explanatory variables. These analyses revealed that even after adjustment for the disease-influencing effects of these covariates, the B*57-NPD genotypes remained strong independent predictors of a slow rate of disease progression (Table 4, models 2 to 10). By contrast, the rates of disease progression among those categorized to B*57-PD and those lacking a B*57 allele were not statistically different (Table 4, model 1), and this association remained after inclusion of the other covariates in the model (Table 4, models 2 to 10).
###end p 76
###begin title 77
Discussion
###end title 77
###begin p 78
###xml 187 192 187 192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ZNRD1</italic>
###xml 292 299 292 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-A10</italic>
###xml 359 365 359 365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-C5</italic>
###xml 442 447 442 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-C</italic>
###xml 452 456 452 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B*57</italic>
